What Is Kalam?
intermediate

Definition of al-Ma'dum and Refutation of Initial Objections
Definition of al-ma'dum and refutation of two objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct definition of the concept of al-ma'dum as a restrictive mental composition and how the author answers the first two objections.

Core Idea
The concept of the nonexistent is a mental distinction, not an external entity.

This passage addresses a critical conceptual foundation in kalam: the meaning of 'nonexistent' (al-ma'dum). The author clarifies that when we speak of the nonexistent, we refer to a concept in the mind, not a thing in the world. He then rebuts two objections based on the most evident necessary truths, showing how the confusion arises from conflating the concept with its supposed external counterpart.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the initial answer
The author starts by stating that what is conceptualized is the concept of the nonexistent, not an external entity. Locate this statement.
2
Understand the definition of the concept
The concept is defined as 'a thing to which non-existence is attributed' as a restrictive composition. Understand why this does not imply an external entity.
The author explicitly denies that it implies an external existent.
3
Examine the two objections and their refutation
The author addresses two objections regarding the most evident necessary truths. See how he distinguishes between the entity and the concept.
The key is the distinction between the mental concept and any supposed external referent.
4
Conclude with the verbal dispute point
The passage mentions that the dispute between the two groups is verbal, and that the concept of the nonexistent is distinguished and established in the mind.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أجوبة الوجوه الثلاثة فقال : ( والجواب إن المتصور مفهوم المعدوم) وذلك لأن المعدوم وقع هناك محمولاً، فيراد به مفهومه (وهو) أي مفهوم المعدوم مفهوم قولنا ( ذات ما ثبت له العدم ) على أنه تركيب تقييدي ( لا ) أي ليس مفهوم المعدوم ( أن ثمة ذاتاً ثبت له العدم في نفس الأمر وإلا اقتضى مفهوم المعدوم تحقق ذات في نفس الأمر متصفة بالعدم فيها وأنه باطل (وهو) أي مفهوم المعدوم هو (المتميز) لكونه المقاصد، والمعدوم بما لا وجود له أصلاً، وأن النزاع بين الفريقين لفظي وهو المذكور في شرح لكن قوله عن قريب يأبى عنه وأما إشارة إلى ما ذكره في جواب الشبهة الرابعة من أن البديهي ما يجزم به بعد تصور الطرفين والنسبة فلعل فيه خللاً، فيتطرق إليه الخطأ بهذا السبب، فلا يلزم رفع الثقة عن البديهيات التي تصور أطرافها كما هو حقها، لكن هذا ينافي كون هذا التصديق من أجلى البديهيات، اللهم إلا أن يقال : إن ذلك قول القادح وليس مسلماً عند المجيب . متصوراً ولكونه محكوماً عليه بالانفصال بينه وبين الموجود (و) هو (الثابت) لكونه متميزاً وهذا الذي ذكره جواب عن الوجهين الأولين وتوضيحه أن يقال : إن أردتم بما ذكرتم في الوجه الأول من أن أجلي البديهيات يتوقف على تصور المعدوم أنه يتوقف على تصور ذات المعدوم، فهو ممنوع وإن أردتم به توقفه على تصور مفهوم المعدوم فهو مسلم ويلزم حينئذ أن يكون مفهوم المعدوم متميزاً وثابتاً في الذهن، ولا استحالة فيه إنما المستحيل أن يكون ما صدق عليه مفهوم المعدوم المطلق ثابتا بوجه، وإن أردتم بما ذكرتم في الوجه الثاني من أن أجلى البديهيات يقتضي تميز المعدوم عن الموجود أنه يقتضي تميز ذات المعدوم المطلق، حتى يلزم أن يكون ذاته ثابتاً ما منعناه، وإن أردتم به أنه يقتضي تميز مفهوم المعدوم المطلق كما هو الظاهر من عبارتكم سلمناه، فيكون لمفهومه حقيقة وللعقل سلبها، فهناك عدم خاص قد عرض لمفهوم المعدوم مطلقاً، وليس في ذلك كون قسم من الشيء قسيماً له، وإنما يلزم هذا
The answers to the three aspects: He said: (The answer is that what is conceptualized is the concept of the nonexistent) because the nonexistent occurred there as a predicate, so by it its concept is intended. (And it) i.e. the concept of the nonexistent is the concept of our saying 'a thing to which non-existence is attributed' as a restrictive composition. (No) i.e. the concept of the nonexistent is not that there is an entity to which non-existence is attributed in the external world, because then the concept of the nonexistent would entail the realization of an entity in the external world described by non-existence, and that is false. (And it) i.e. the concept of the nonexistent is what is distinguished. ... [And the nonexistent is what has no existence at all, and the dispute between the two groups is verbal, as mentioned in the commentary...] ... being conceptualized and because it is judged by separation between it and the existent, and it is the established due to being distinguished. This which he mentioned is an answer to the first two aspects, and its clarification is that it is said: If you mean by what you mentioned in the first aspect that the most evident of the necessary truths depends on the conceptualization of the nonexistent, that it depends on the conceptualization of the entity of the nonexistent, then it is denied. But if you mean by it its dependence on the conceptualization of the concept of the nonexistent, then it is granted. Then it follows that the concept of the nonexistent is distinguished and established in the mind, and there is no impossibility in that. What is impossible is that what is predicated by the absolute concept of the nonexistent should be established in any way. And if you mean by what you mentioned in the second aspect that the most evident of the necessary truths requires the distinction of the nonexistent from the existent, that it requires the distinction of the entity of the absolute nonexistent, so that its essence be established, then we deny it. But if you mean by it that it requires the distinction of the concept of the absolute nonexistent, as is apparent from your expression, then we grant it. So its concept has a reality and the mind has its negation, so there is a specific non-existence that has occurred to the concept of the absolute nonexistent, and in that there is not a part of the thing being its opposite, but rather this would follow [only if...]
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof-like response to objections concerning the concept of al-ma'dum (the nonexistent). The author begins by stating the answer to three aspects (objections): that what is conceptualized is the concept of the nonexistent, not an external nonexistent entity. He explains that the term 'ma'dum' when used as a predicate refers to its concept, which is a restrictive composition: 'a thing to which non-existence is attributed.' This composition does not imply the existence of an actual entity in the external world described by non-existence, because that would be contradictory. Rather, the concept of the nonexistent is simply a mental distinction. The author then addresses two specific objections. In the first objection, it is claimed that the most evident necessary truths depend on conceptualizing the nonexistent. The author distinguishes: if one means the entity of the nonexistent, it is denied; if one means the concept, it is granted and entails that the concept is distinct and established in the mind without impossibility. The impossibility is only if the absolute concept were realized externally. In the second objection about distinguishing the nonexistent from the existent, similarly, if one means the entity, it is denied; if one means the concept, it is granted, and the concept has reality while the mind negates it externally, avoiding contradiction. The passage thus clarifies that the concept of the nonexistent is a valid mental object without external existence.

Key Terms
معدوم
مفهوم
تركيب تقييدي
بديهيات
متميز
ثابت
عدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some argue that the concept of al-ma'dum implies an actual external entity that possesses non-existence.
Correction: The author explains that the concept is merely a mental restrictive composition with no external counterpart; the absolute concept of the nonexistent cannot be externally realized.

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the correct understanding of the concept of al-ma'dum?
A) It refers to an actual entity in the external world that has non-existence.
B) It is a restrictive composition (tarkib taqyidi) that exists only in the mind as a concept.
C) It is a verbal dispute with no real meaning.
D) It is a necessary truth that must be accepted without analysis.

Key Takeaway
The concept of al-ma'dum is a mental restrictive composition that does not refer to any external entity, and the confusion in objections arises from conflating the concept with its supposed external referent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about 'nothingness' or 'nonexistence' in your own life—like things that have passed or not yet come—do you treat them as real in your mind? How might the lesson's distinction between concept and external reality change the way you emotionally attach to what is absent?
?
The author argues that even the most evident truths depend on a concept of the nonexistent. Can you identify a belief you hold so firmly that you have never examined its conceptual foundations? Would you be willing to test that belief by distinguishing between its mental concept and its actual external referent?

The Four Main Stages of Human Life
Jurjani enumerates the four main stages of human life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four major stages of human life as classified by Jurjani: the age of growth, the age of stability, the age of manhood (hidden decline), and the age of old age (apparent decline).

Core Idea
Human life progresses through four stages: growth, stability, hidden decline, and apparent decline.

Jurjani begins by outlining the broadest classification of human life. He identifies four major ages that capture the arc from birth to death: the age of growth, the age of stability, the age of decline with remaining strength (manhood), and the age of decline with weakness (old age). This framework provides a clear structure for understanding the natural progression of human development.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening definitions
Notice how Jurjani defines 'walid' and 'tifl' before presenting the four stages. This sets the stage for the classification.
2
Identify the four stages
List the four ages: sinn al-numu, sinn al-wuquf, kuhula, shaykhukha. Note the approximate ages given for each.
Pay attention to the qualifying phrases about decline.
3
Understand the logic
Ask: Why are there two stages of decline? The difference is the presence or absence of strength. This is a nuanced observation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فكان وليداً) أي مولوداً ثم طفلاً، الأسنان أربعة سن النمو، ويسمى سن وهو إلى قريب من ثلاثين سنة، ثم سن الوقوف وهو سن الشباب وهو إلى نحو من خمس وثلاثين سنة أو أربعين ثم سن الانحطاط مع بقاء القوة وهو سن الكهولة، وهو إلى نحو من ستين سنة، ثم سن الانحطاط مع ظهور ضعف في القوة سن الشيخوخة إلى آخر العمر، وسن الحداثة ينقسم إلى سن الطفولة وهو أن يكون المولود غير مستعد الأعضاء للحركة والنهوض، ثم وهو بعد النهوض وقبل الشدة، وهو أن يكون الأسنان قد استوفت السقوط والنبات، ثم سن سن الترعرع وهو بعد الشدة ونبات الأسنان قبل المراهقة، ثم سن الغلامية والرهاق إلى أن يبقل وجهه ثم سن الفتى إلى أن يقف النمو . الصبا قوله : ( أي تحرك ونشأ مدته في الأغلب إلى ثمانية وعشرين وقيل إلى خمسة وثلاثين بدليل زيادة الجمال والقوة وعود الطواحين الساقطة بعد العشرين وأما مدة الكهولة وهي التي يكون النقصان فيها خفياً، فهي من خمسة وثلاثين وقيل من أربعين إلى ستين، ومدة الشيخوخة وهي التي يكون النقصان فيها ظاهراً من آخر الكهولة إلى ما يشاء الله تعالى، وتفصيله موكول إلى موضعه .
His statement: '(So he was a walid)' i.e., born, then a child. The ages are four: the age of growth, which is called 'sinn' and extends to near thirty years; then the age of stability, which is the age of youth (shabab) extending to about thirty-five or forty years; then the age of decline with remaining strength, which is the age of manhood (kuhula) extending to about sixty years; then the age of decline with the appearance of weakness in strength, which is the age of old age (shaykhukha) until the end of life. The age of childhood (hadatha) is divided into: the age of infancy (tufula), when the newborn's limbs are not ready for movement and rising; then (the age) after rising and before strength (shidda), when the teeth have completed falling and growing; then the age of groping (tar'ur'u'), which is after strength and the growth of teeth before puberty; then the age of boyhood (ghulamya) and approaching puberty (rahaq) until his face sprouts down; then the age of youth (fata) until growth stops. 'Sabah': His statement: '(i.e., he moved and grew), its duration is mostly up to twenty-eight, and it is said up to thirty-five, as evidenced by the increase of beauty and strength and the return of fallen molars after twenty. As for the duration of manhood (kuhula), in which the decline is hidden, it is from thirty-five, or it is said from forty, to sixty. And the duration of old age (shaykhukha), in which the decline is apparent, is from the end of manhood to whatever God wills. The detailed account is relegated to its proper place.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a classification and definition of the stages of human life. It begins by explaining that the term 'walid' means 'born', then 'tifl' (child). It then enumerates four main stages: 1) the age of growth (sin al-numu), extending to about thirty years; 2) the age of stability (sin al-wuquf), which is youth (shabab), up to about thirty-five or forty; 3) the age of decline with remaining strength (sin al-inhitat ma'a baqa' al-quwwa), which is manhood (kuhula), up to about sixty; 4) the age of decline with weakness (sin al-inhitat ma'a zuhur da'f), which is old age (shaykhukha) until the end of life. The passage then subdivides the period of childhood (hadatha) into infancy (tufula), then the stage after rising and before strength, then the stage of groping (tar'ur'u') after strength and before puberty, then boyhood (ghulamya) and approaching puberty, then youth (fata) until growth stops. It also provides durations: sabah (youthful vigor) mostly up to twenty-eight or thirty-five, manhood from thirty-five or forty to sixty, and old age from the end of manhood to the end of life. The author notes that the full details are left to their proper place.

Key Terms
النمو
الوقوف
الكهولة
الشيخوخة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think 'sinn' refers to teeth rather than stages of life.
Correction: Here 'sinn' is used in the sense of age or stage, not teeth.

Checkpoint
According to this classification, which stage is defined by the appearance of weakness in strength?
A) Age of growth
B) Age of stability
C) Manhood (kuhula)
D) Old age (shaykhukha)

Key Takeaway
Human life is divided into four main stages: growth, youth/stability, manhood with hidden decline, and old age with apparent decline.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read about the four stages of life. Which stage are you in right now? Have you ever consciously acknowledged that you are moving steadily toward decline and death? If not, what one concrete action will you take today to prepare for the next stage?
?
If you are in the stage of stability or decline, ask yourself: What have I built that will remain after I leave this world? This lesson forces you to see the clock. Are you using your remaining time for what truly matters, or are you drifting?
?
The passage says the third stage (kuhula) is when strength remains but decline has begun. If you are there, what are you hiding from yourself? If you are younger, what can you learn from those older? Will you wait for weakness to force you to change?

Subdivisions of Childhood and Durations of Life Stages
Jurjani subdivides childhood and provides durations for the main life stages.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the subdivisions of childhood (hadatha) and the specific durations for sabah, kuhula, and shaykhukha.

Core Idea
Childhood has five distinct phases, and the main stages have defined durations.

After outlining the four major stages, Jurjani provides a more detailed breakdown of the childhood period (hadatha). He also gives specific durations for the period of youthful vigor (sabah), manhood (kuhula), and old age (shaykhukha), along with evidence for some claims.

Guided Path
1
Read the subdivisions of childhood
Identify the five phases: infancy, after rising, tar'ur'u', ghulamya, and fata. Note how each is defined.
These phases are based on physical development.
2
Examine the durations
Look at the durations given for sabah (growth), kuhula, and shaykhukha. Note the disagreements and the evidence mentioned for sabah.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Ask: Why does Jurjani provide such detailed subdivisions? This reflects the systematic nature of Islamic scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( فكان وليداً) أي مولوداً ثم طفلاً، الأسنان أربعة سن النمو، ويسمى سن وهو إلى قريب من ثلاثين سنة، ثم سن الوقوف وهو سن الشباب وهو إلى نحو من خمس وثلاثين سنة أو أربعين ثم سن الانحطاط مع بقاء القوة وهو سن الكهولة، وهو إلى نحو من ستين سنة، ثم سن الانحطاط مع ظهور ضعف في القوة سن الشيخوخة إلى آخر العمر، وسن الحداثة ينقسم إلى سن الطفولة وهو أن يكون المولود غير مستعد الأعضاء للحركة والنهوض، ثم وهو بعد النهوض وقبل الشدة، وهو أن يكون الأسنان قد استوفت السقوط والنبات، ثم سن سن الترعرع وهو بعد الشدة ونبات الأسنان قبل المراهقة، ثم سن الغلامية والرهاق إلى أن يبقل وجهه ثم سن الفتى إلى أن يقف النمو . الصبا قوله : ( أي تحرك ونشأ مدته في الأغلب إلى ثمانية وعشرين وقيل إلى خمسة وثلاثين بدليل زيادة الجمال والقوة وعود الطواحين الساقطة بعد العشرين وأما مدة الكهولة وهي التي يكون النقصان فيها خفياً، فهي من خمسة وثلاثين وقيل من أربعين إلى ستين، ومدة الشيخوخة وهي التي يكون النقصان فيها ظاهراً من آخر الكهولة إلى ما يشاء الله تعالى، وتفصيله موكول إلى موضعه .
His statement: '(So he was a walid)' i.e., born, then a child. The ages are four: the age of growth, which is called 'sinn' and extends to near thirty years; then the age of stability, which is the age of youth (shabab) extending to about thirty-five or forty years; then the age of decline with remaining strength, which is the age of manhood (kuhula) extending to about sixty years; then the age of decline with the appearance of weakness in strength, which is the age of old age (shaykhukha) until the end of life. The age of childhood (hadatha) is divided into: the age of infancy (tufula), when the newborn's limbs are not ready for movement and rising; then (the age) after rising and before strength (shidda), when the teeth have completed falling and growing; then the age of groping (tar'ur'u'), which is after strength and the growth of teeth before puberty; then the age of boyhood (ghulamya) and approaching puberty (rahaq) until his face sprouts down; then the age of youth (fata) until growth stops. 'Sabah': His statement: '(i.e., he moved and grew), its duration is mostly up to twenty-eight, and it is said up to thirty-five, as evidenced by the increase of beauty and strength and the return of fallen molars after twenty. As for the duration of manhood (kuhula), in which the decline is hidden, it is from thirty-five, or it is said from forty, to sixty. And the duration of old age (shaykhukha), in which the decline is apparent, is from the end of manhood to whatever God wills. The detailed account is relegated to its proper place.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is a classification and definition of the stages of human life. It begins by explaining that the term 'walid' means 'born', then 'tifl' (child). It then enumerates four main stages: 1) the age of growth (sin al-numu), extending to about thirty years; 2) the age of stability (sin al-wuquf), which is youth (shabab), up to about thirty-five or forty; 3) the age of decline with remaining strength (sin al-inhitat ma'a baqa' al-quwwa), which is manhood (kuhula), up to about sixty; 4) the age of decline with weakness (sin al-inhitat ma'a zuhur da'f), which is old age (shaykhukha) until the end of life. The passage then subdivides the period of childhood (hadatha) into infancy (tufula), then the stage after rising and before strength, then the stage of groping (tar'ur'u') after strength and before puberty, then boyhood (ghulamya) and approaching puberty, then youth (fata) until growth stops. It also provides durations: sabah (youthful vigor) mostly up to twenty-eight or thirty-five, manhood from thirty-five or forty to sixty, and old age from the end of manhood to the end of life. The author notes that the full details are left to their proper place.

What evidence is given for the duration of sabah being up to thirty-five?
A) Increase of wisdom

Childhood is subdivided into five phases, and the life stages have defined durations with some scholarly disagreement.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of these stages are you currently in? If you are in the prime or decline phase, what specific signs (like the return of molars or the appearance of weakness) have you actually observed in yourself, and how do they align with what Jurjani teaches? Write a concrete plan to use your remaining time accordingly.
?
The duration of old age is described as 'to whatever Allah wills' — no fixed number. How does this uncertainty about your own lifespan challenge your current life priorities? What is one thing you will do today to prepare for a long or sudden old age, acting on this lesson?
?
You have just learned that each stage has specific biological markers and durations. Does your current daily routine reflect that you are in a specific stage, and if not, what changes must you make immediately to live in accordance with the natural order Allah has set?

Two Interpretations of the Purpose of al-Nazar
Al-Jurjani discusses two interpretations of the purpose of al-nazar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two interpretations of the purpose of al-nazar (rational consideration) and why the interpretation related to establishing religious beliefs is more appropriate for the science of kalam.

Core Idea
The purpose of al-nazar is twofold: establishing religious beliefs and knowing Allah.

Al-Jurjani introduces the Fifth Observatory on al-nazar, explaining that it is the means to achieve a desired goal. He presents two interpretations of that goal: one specific to the science of kalam (establishing religious beliefs) and another rooted in the purpose of human creation (knowledge of Allah). This lesson unpacks both views and clarifies why the first is preferred in this context.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the translation. Notice the two interpretations and the Quranic evidence cited.
2
Identify the two interpretations
Find where al-Jurjani states the first interpretation (establishment of religious beliefs) and the second (knowledge of Allah). Note how each is supported.
The first is attributed to the science of kalam; the second is supported by a Quranic verse and Ibn Abbas's commentary.
3
Understand the preferred interpretation
Look at the commentary: it says the first interpretation is 'more apparent and appropriate' for the context. Ask yourself why that might be the case.
This connects to the purpose of the book: to provide a science that can defend and establish creed.
4
Consider the rebuttal
Al-Jurjani addresses a potential objection: could the difference be about the subject matter of kalam? He argues that this does not justify specification, because kalam is about establishing religious beliefs regardless of its subject.
This shows the commentator's careful reasoning.

المرصد الخامس في النظر إذ به يحصل المطلوب الذي هو إثبات العقائد الدينية ، وقيل : هو معرفة الله تعالى ( وفيه مقاصد ) . قوله : ( الذي هو إثبات إلخ) بأن يراد بالمطلوب المطلوب من علم الكلام، وهو الأظهر المناسب لا يراد مباحث النظر فيه . قوله : ( وقيل هو معرفة الله تعالى بأن يراد به المطلوب من خلقة الإنسان قال الله تعالى : ﴿ وما خلقت الجن والإنس إلا ليعبدون ﴾ [الذاريات : ٥٦] قال ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما : أي ليعرفون وحمل التوجيهين على الاختلاف في موضوع الفن بأنه المعلوم أو ذاته تعالى لا يظهر به وجه التخصيص، فإن الكلام علم يقتدر به على إثبات العقائد الدينية أي شيء كان موضوعه .
The Fifth Observatory: On al-Nazar (consideration), for by it is attained the desired goal, which is the establishment of religious beliefs, and it is said: it is knowledge of Allah the Exalted. (And it contains aims). His statement: (which is the establishment, etc.) meaning that by 'the desired goal' is meant the desired goal of the science of kalam, and it is the more apparent and appropriate; the investigations of al-nazar itself are not meant. His statement: (and it is said: it is knowledge of Allah the Exalted) meaning that by it is meant the desired goal of human creation. Allah the Exalted said: 'And I did not create the jinn and mankind except to worship Me' [Quran 51:56]. Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, said: meaning to know Me. And carrying the two interpretations on the difference concerning the subject matter of the art—whether it is the known thing or His Essence the Exalted—does not show a basis for specification, for kalam is a science by which one is able to establish religious beliefs, whatever its subject matter may be.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage introduces the Fifth Observatory on al-Nazar (rational consideration). It first states two interpretations of the purpose (al-matlub) of al-nazar: the first is the establishment of religious beliefs (the goal of ilm al-kalam), and the second is knowledge of Allah (the goal of human creation, as per the Quranic verse). The commentary explains that the first interpretation is more apparent and appropriate for the context of kalam. It then addresses a potential objection: the difference between these two interpretations might be based on whether the subject matter of kalam is 'the known thing' or 'the Essence of Allah'. The commentator concludes that this does not justify specification, because kalam is a science that enables the establishment of religious beliefs regardless of its subject matter.

Key Terms
النظر
المطلوب
العقائد الدينية
معرفة الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The two interpretations of the purpose of al-nazar are contradictory or imply a fundamental disagreement about the nature of kalam.
Correction: They are not contradictory: one refers to the specific goal of kalam (establishing religious beliefs), the other to the ultimate purpose of human creation (knowing Allah). They operate on different levels.

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, what is the more appropriate interpretation of 'al-matlub' in the context of the Fifth Observatory?
A) Knowledge of Allah
B) Establishment of religious beliefs
C) The subject matter of kalam
D) The act of worship

Key Takeaway
Within the science of kalam, the primary purpose of al-nazar is to establish religious beliefs, even though a broader religious purpose is to know Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you engage in studying 'ilm al-kalam, do you ever lose sight of the ultimate purpose of knowing Allah? How does this passage remind you that the immediate goal of establishing beliefs must always serve the deeper purpose of ma'rifah? What one change will you make in your study habits to keep both purposes aligned?
?
The passage distinguishes between the goal of kalam (establishing beliefs) and the goal of creation (knowing Allah). Which of these two has been driving your pursuit of Islamic knowledge? If you are honest, is your study of 'aqeedah merely to win arguments or to truly know your Lord? How will you transform your intention today?

Al-Baqillani's Definition of Nazar and the First Objection
Al-Jurjani presents al-Baqillani's definition of nazar and explains the first objection regarding non-matching conjecture.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Baqillani's definition of nazar as thought seeking knowledge or predominant conjecture, and the first objection that this definition would entail seeking ignorance, as well as the response that the intended conjecture is only that which matches reality.

Core Idea
Nazar seeks only what matches reality, not mere conjecture.

In this passage, al-Jurjani presents al-Baqillani's definition of nazar and the first of four objections raised against it. The objection, attributed to al-Amidi, argues that since conjecture can be false, defining nazar as seeking conjecture would make it seek ignorance. The author (al-Iji) adds that no rational person seeks false conjecture. This lesson unpacks the definition and the objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition and objection
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyze it. Then read the translation. Let the argument's progression come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage begins with the definition and then immediately presents the objection.
2
Understand the definition
Al-Baqillani defines nazar as thought (al-fikr) by which one seeks knowledge or predominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann). Note that it is a means, not an end.
The definition is explicit: 'al-nazar huwa al-fikr alladhi yutlab bihi 'ilm aw ghalabat zann.'
3
Identify the objection's logic
The objection divides conjecture into matching (conforming to reality) and non-matching. Non-matching conjecture is ignorance. So if nazar seeks conjecture (absolute), it seeks ignorance, which is impossible.
4
See how the author defends the definition
Al-Iji adds that no rational person seeks non-matching conjecture. The commentary clarifies that the sought (al-matlab) is only a conjecture known to match reality, not any conjecture.
This resolves the objection by narrowing the intended conjecture.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الأول : في تعريفه ] ( في تعريفه قال القاضي الباقلاني : النظر ) هو الفكر الذي يطلب به علم أو غلبة ظن وأورد عليه أسئلة ( أربعة السؤال ( الأول ) أن الظن ينقسم إلى مطابق وغير مطابق و ( الظن الغير المطابق جهل، فيلزم مما ذكره في تعريف النظر أن يكون الجهل مطلوباً، كذا قال الآمدي وزاد عليه المصنف فقال : ( لا يطلبه عاقل فإذا المطلوب) وهو ممتنع . قوله : (فيلزم مما ذكر في تعريف إلخ من كون الظن المطلق مطلوباً أن يكون الجهل مطلوباً. قوله : ( وهو ممتنع إذ ليس المراد بالجهل هاهنا الجهل المركب لأنه ضد الظن بل عدم العلم بما في الواقع، ولا شك أن عدم العلم يمتنع طلبه طلبه امتناعاً ذاتياً. قوله : ( وزاد عليه إلخ) أشار بذلك إلى أن ما ذكره الآمدي ملحوظ للمصنف أيضاً، إلا أنه تركه لظهوره وزاد عليه وجهاً آخر وهو أن الظن الغير المطابق لا يطلبه عاقل، فقوله : لا يطلبه خبر بعد خبر والضمير راجع إلى الظن الغير المطابق، وليس عطفاً على قوله، والظن الغير المطابق جهل، والضمير عائد إلى الجهل على ما وهم وقيل : إنه المراد بالامتناع في عبارة الآمدي، فالزائد قوله فإذا المطلوب. قوله : وزاد عليه المصنف فقال : إلخ) الزائد أصالة على ما ذكره الآمدي هو التفريع المذكور لا قوله ولا يطلبه عاقل لأن الامتناع الذي ذكره الآمدي يؤول إليه . قوله : ( فإذاً المطلوب بالفكر مظن ما يعلم مطابقته للواقع أي الذي يطلبه المفكر بنظره
The First Aim: On its definition. (In its definition, al-Qadi al-Baqillani said: al-nazar is) the thought by which knowledge or predominant conjecture is sought. And four questions were raised against it. (The first question:) That conjecture is divided into matching and non-matching, and (non-matching conjecture is ignorance, so it follows from what he mentioned in the definition of nazar that ignorance is sought. Thus said al-Amidi, and the author added, saying: (No rational person seeks it, so the sought [i.e., ignorance] is impossible). His statement: (So it follows from what was mentioned in the definition, etc., from the fact that absolute conjecture is sought, that ignorance is sought.) His statement: (And it is impossible, for what is meant by ignorance here is not compound ignorance, for it is the opposite of conjecture, but rather lack of knowledge of what is in reality, and there is no doubt that seeking lack of knowledge is inherently impossible.) His statement: (And he added, etc.) He indicated by that that what al-Amidi mentioned was also noted by the author, except that he left it due to its obviousness and added another aspect: that non-matching conjecture is not sought by a rational person. So his statement 'no rational person seeks it' is a predicate after a predicate, and the pronoun refers to non-matching conjecture, and it is not an conjunction to his statement 'non-matching conjecture is ignorance', and the pronoun refers to ignorance, according to a misunderstanding. And it is said that what is meant by the impossibility in al-Amidi's expression is that, so the added element is his statement 'so the sought'. His statement: (and the author added, saying, etc.) The original addition to what al-Amidi mentioned is the mentioned inference, not his statement 'and no rational person seeks it', because the impossibility that al-Amidi mentioned reduces to it. His statement: (So the sought by thought is a conjecture whose conformity to reality is known, i.e., that which the thinker seeks by his nazar).
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage defines al-nazar and addresses the first objection raised against al-Baqillani's definition. The definition states that nazar is thought by which one seeks knowledge or predominant conjecture (ghalabat al-zann). The first objection, attributed to al-Amidi, is that conjecture is divided into matching (conforming to reality) and non-matching; non-matching conjecture is ignorance. Therefore, if nazar seeks absolute conjecture, it would entail seeking ignorance, which is impossible. The author (al-Iji) adds that no rational person seeks non-matching conjecture. The commentary explains that the impossibility lies in seeking ignorance as lack of knowledge, which is inherently impossible. It clarifies that the intended 'conjecture' in the definition is what is thought to match reality, not absolute conjecture.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection believes that al-Baqillani's definition of nazar aims at any conjecture, including false ones.
Correction: Al-Baqillani only intends conjecture that is known to match reality (mutabiq).

Checkpoint

A) Nazar seeks both knowledge and conjecture, which are contradictory
B) Because conjecture can be false, nazar would aim at ignorance
C) Nazar cannot be defined as thought
D) The definition is too broad

Key Takeaway
Al-Baqillani's definition of nazar must be understood as seeking only conjecture that is known to be true, not any conjecture.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You claim to seek the truth through nazar, but have you ever pursued a belief simply because it felt comfortable, knowing it might not match reality? What does al-Baqillani's definition expose about your intent?
?
The objection shows that no rational person seeks ignorance. Why, then, do you sometimes turn away from evidence that contradicts your preferences? What are you protecting?
?
If nazar only aims at what matches reality, your thoughts must be constantly checked against the truth. When was the last time you changed a deeply held opinion because new evidence disproved it? Are you truly open to being corrected today?

The Definition of Nazar and the First Objection
Al-Iji and al-Baqillani define nazar, then present the first objection and its answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of speculative thought (nazar) and the first objection concerning the inclusion of conjecture, and how scholars resolved it.

Core Idea
Speculative thought seeks the truth, not any conjecture.

This lesson presents the foundational definition of nazar (speculative thought) as the means to establish religious doctrines. It then examines a powerful objection: if nazar seeks conjecture, and conjecture can be false, then nazar would seemingly seek ignorance. The resolution clarifies that nazar only seeks conjecture that is either known to correspond to reality or is pursued as such in practical reasoning, thus avoiding the absurdity.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of nazar
Read the opening lines where al-Baqillani defines nazar as thought seeking knowledge or preponderant conjecture. Notice the alternative view that it is knowledge of God.
The definition sets up the objection.
2
Understand the objection
The objection argues that since conjecture includes non-corresponding conjecture (ignorance), seeking conjecture would mean seeking ignorance. Identify why this is a problem.
The key is the division of conjecture into corresponding and non-corresponding.
3
Follow the response
The response distinguishes between absolute conjecture and non-corresponding conjecture. The author explains that the sought conjecture is either known to be true or is sought regardless of correspondence in practical ijtihad. Thus, seeking ignorance does not follow.
Notice that the response uses the concept of 'practical ijtihādāt' as a counterexample.

The Fifth Observatory on Speculative Thought (al-nazar), for through it the desired objective is obtained, which is the establishment of religious doctrines, and it is said: it is knowledge of God Most High. (And it contains aims.) The First Aim: On its Definition. (On its definition, al-Qadi al-Baqillani said: al-nazar) is the thought (al-fikr) by which knowledge (ʿilm) or preponderant conjecture (ghalabat ẓann) is sought. And four objections were raised against it. The First Objection: that conjecture (al-ẓann) divides into that which is corresponding (muṭābiq) and non-corresponding (ghayr muṭābiq), and (non-corresponding conjecture is ignorance (jahl)), so it necessarily follows from what he mentioned in the definition of speculative thought that ignorance is sought. Thus said al-Amidi, and the author added to it and said: (No rational person seeks it, so the sought (al-maṭlūb) is impossible.) His saying: (which is the establishment, etc.) meaning that what is intended by 'the sought' is what is sought from the science of kalām, and it is the more apparent and appropriate; the investigations of speculative thought itself are not intended. His saying: (and it is said: it is knowledge of God Most High) meaning that what is intended by it is what is sought from the creation of man. God Most High said: {And I did not create the jinn and mankind except to worship Me} [Quran 51:56]. Ibn Abbas, may God be pleased with them both, said: meaning to know Me. And carrying the two interpretations on the difference regarding the subject matter of the art—whether it is the known (al-maʿlūm) or His Essence Most High—does not appear as a specification, for kalām is a science by which one can establish religious doctrines regardless of its subject matter. His saying: (so it necessarily follows from what was mentioned in the definition, etc.) that from the fact that absolute conjecture is sought, it follows that ignorance is sought. His saying: (And it is impossible, for what is meant by ignorance here is not compound ignorance (al-jahl al-murakkab) because it is the opposite of conjecture, but rather the absence of knowledge of what is in reality, and there is no doubt that the absence of knowledge cannot be sought; seeking it is intrinsically impossible.) His saying: (And he added to it, etc.) He indicated by that that what al-Amidi mentioned is also noted by the author, except that he left it due to its obviousness and added another aspect: that non-corresponding conjecture is not sought by any rational person. Thus his saying: 'He does not seek it' is a predicate after a predicate, and the pronoun refers to non-corresponding conjecture, and it is not a conjunction on his saying, and non-corresponding conjecture is ignorance, and the pronoun refers back to ignorance as some have erroneously thought, and it is said that it is what is meant by impossibility in al-Amidi's expression, so the additional part is his saying 'so the sought'. His saying: (which is the establishment of religious doctrines) this is more appropriate to what the author held, that the subject matter of kalām is the known inasmuch as it pertains to the establishment of religious doctrines, and therefore he preferred it over the second opinion, which is more appropriate to making its subject matter the Essence of God Most High, as detailed previously. His saying: (And the author added to it and said, etc.) The additional element fundamentally beyond what al-Amidi mentioned is the aforementioned deduction, not his saying 'nor does a rational person seek it', because the impossibility that al-Amidi mentioned leads to it. His saying: (So the sought through thought is a conjecture whose correspondence to reality is known) i.e., that which the thinker seeks through his thought from conjecture (and that whose correspondence to reality is known) so it becomes knowledge (ʿilm), not conjecture. Then his saying 'or preponderant conjecture' becomes redundant. And it can be said: perhaps he is satisfied with conjecture of correspondence, so it is not included in knowledge, so there is no redundancy. We said: Rather, he seeks conjecture (insofar as it is conjecture, without regard to its correspondence) to the conjectured (and its lack), for the primary objective may be based on conjecture as conjecture, as in practical ijtihādāt (independent reasoning). And from seeking the more general, which is absolute conjecture, it does not follow (seeking the more specific, which is non-corresponding conjecture), so seeking ignorance does not follow.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage combines the introductory definition of speculative thought (al-nazar) and the first objection raised against it, along with the full response. The passage is structured as a dialectical argument: definition, objection, and refutation. 

The author begins by stating that the Fifth Observatory concerns al-nazar, through which the desired objective—establishing religious doctrines—is attained. An alternative view is that the objective is knowledge of God Most High. Then the First Aim is introduced: the definition of nazar. Al-Qadi al-Baqillani defines nazar as 'the thought by which knowledge or preponderant conjecture is sought.' Four objections are raised; the first is presented here. 

The objection: Conjecture (al-ẓann) divides into two types: corresponding to reality (muṭābiq) and non-corresponding (ghayr muṭābiq). Non-corresponding conjecture is ignorance. If nazar seeks either knowledge or conjecture, and conjecture includes the non-corresponding type, then nazar would seek ignorance—something no rational person seeks. Thus the definition is flawed. Al-Amidi first pointed this out, and the author (al-musannif) added: 'No rational person seeks it, so the sought is impossible,' meaning that since ignorance is not sought, the definition cannot intend absolute conjecture. 

The commentator then explains each phrase. He clarifies that the 'sought' in the definition refers to what kalām seeks, not the internal investigations of nazar. The alternative view ('knowledge of God') aligns with the Quranic verse about creation for worship, interpreted as knowledge. The commentator argues that the two interpretations do not affect the subject matter of kalām. 

On the impossibility of seeking ignorance, the commentator specifies that 'ignorance' here is not compound ignorance (which is a positive belief contrary to reality) but simple ignorance—the absence of knowledge. Seeking such absence is inherently impossible. The author's addition is then explained: the additional aspect is the explicit statement that non-corresponding conjecture is not sought by any rational person. The pronoun in 'he does not seek it' refers to that non-corresponding conjecture. 

Finally, the commentator refines the definition by arguing that what is actually sought through nazar is a conjecture whose correspondence to reality is known after it is obtained—thus it becomes knowledge, not conjecture. This would make the phrase 'or preponderant conjecture' redundant. However, an alternative response is considered: perhaps one can be satisfied with mere conjecture of correspondence, without certain knowledge. The commentator then presents the author's own position: 'Rather, he seeks conjecture insofar as it is conjecture, without regard to its correspondence or lack thereof.' This is because practical rulings in ijtihad are based on preponderant conjecture as such, regardless of actual correspondence. Therefore, seeking absolute conjecture does not entail seeking non-corresponding conjecture, so the objection is refuted.

Key Terms
نظر (nazar)
ظن (zann)
علم (ʿilm)
جهل (jahl)
مطابق (muṭābiq)
غير مطابق (ghayr muṭābiq)
الاجتهاديات العملية (al-ijtihādiyyāt al-ʿamaliyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The definition of nazar includes all conjecture, even false ones.
Correction: The definition only intends conjecture that is either known to correspond to reality or is sought as conjecture for practical purposes.

Checkpoint
What is the first objection against al-Baqillani's definition of nazar?
A) It contradicts the Quran.
B) It implies that ignorance is sought because conjecture includes non-corresponding conjecture, which is ignorance.
C) It is too narrow and excludes practical reasoning.
D) It relies on an invalid analogy.

Key Takeaway
Speculative thought (nazar) seeks either certain knowledge or preponderant conjecture that is relevant to religious doctrines, not mere guesswork.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about your faith, do you honestly seek certain knowledge ('ilm) or are you often content with mere conjecture (zann)? Which areas of your belief need more rigorous investigation?
?
The objection warns that seeking false conjecture is impossible for a rational person. Have you ever held a belief about God or religion that you knew might be based on weak evidence? What would it take for you to abandon such a belief and pursue certainty?
?
The lesson distinguishes between seeking conjecture for its own sake (as in practical ijtihad) versus as a means to knowledge. In your daily religious practice, do you sometimes rely on guesses or habits instead of striving for understanding? How can you shift from passive acceptance to active inquiry?

The Object of Thought: A Preponderant Opinion
Objection-and-answer on the object of thought

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what is truly sought by rational thought (al-fikr) in Islamic theology and ijtihad: a preponderant opinion based on evidence, not necessarily knowledge of its correspondence to reality.

Core Idea
The goal of thought is a well-grounded opinion, not certainty of correspondence.

This passage delves into an objection about the object of thought. At first, it seems thought aims for a matching opinion whose accuracy is known. But the commentator reveals that the real goal, especially in practical ijtihad, is a preponderant belief based on evidence, without requiring knowledge of correspondence. This distinction clarifies the nature of theological reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once through, then the English translation. Let the flow of the objection and response sink in before analyzing.
2
Identify the initial claim and rationale
The commentator first states that the object sought by thought is a matching opinion whose correspondence is known after it occurs. Note the rationale: if correspondence were not known, a non-matching opinion could be sought, which is false.
3
Understand the objection
The objector challenges: why must the opinion's correspondence be known? Could it not be merely conjectured? Pay attention to the phrase 'قد يكتفي'.
4
Follow the commentator's response
The commentator rejects the implication. He argues that what is sought is the opinion of the ruling insofar as it is a preponderant belief (zann), without regard to its correspondence. This is shown by the example of ijtihad.
Notice the shift with 'بل'.
5
Reflect on the difference between the two answers
The commentator concludes by highlighting that his answer differs from the author's. Reflect on how they diverge: one emphasizes known correspondence, the other emphasizes preponderant belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإذاً المطلوب بالفكر إلخ) أي المطلوب بالفكر هو الظن المطابق الذي يعلم مطابقته بعد حصوله، إذ لو لم يعلم مطابقته بعد حصوله لاحتمل أن يكون غير مطابق، فيلزم كون الغير المطابق مطلوباً في الجملة وقد بان بطلانه . قوله: (فيكون علماً لكونه جزماً مطابقاً للواقع ضرورة أن ما يعلم مطابقته تجزم به النفس . قوله : (قد يكتفي) أي لا نسلم أن المطلوب بالفكر هو الظن المعلوم مطابقته، لم لا يجوز أن يكون الظن المطابق ؟ الذي يظن مطابقته بعد حصوله . قوله: (قلنا بل يطلب إلخ إضراب عن مقدر أي لا نسلم أنه إذا لم يكن الظن الغير المطابق مطلوباً، يلزم أن يكون الظن المطابق الذي يعلم مطابقته مطلوبا، بل يطلب بالنظر في الدليل الظن بالحكم من حيث أنه ظن أي اعتقاد راجح بالنظر إليه من غير التفات إلى مطابقته وعدم مطابقته فإن المقصود الأصلي كالعمل في الاجتهاديات قد يترتب على الظن بالحكم بالنظر إلى الدليل، فإن الحكم الذي غلب على ظن المجتهد كونه مستفاداً من الدليل يجب العمل به عليه من غير التفات إلى مطابقته وعدم مطابقته سيما عند من يقول أن كل مجتهد مصيب، ولذا يثاب المجتهد المخطئ أيضاً، وقد ظهر بما حررنا لك الفرق بين جواب الشارح وجواب المصنف، بما لا مزيد عليه وأن القول باتحادهما في المال وهم .
His saying: (So the object sought by thought) i.e. the object sought by thought is the matching opinion whose correspondence is known after it occurs, because if its correspondence were not known after it occurs, it would be possible that it is non-matching, and thus the non-matching would be sought in some respect, and its falsehood has become clear. His saying: (Thus it is knowledge because it is a decisive judgment matching reality, necessarily because what is known to correspond, the soul judges it decisively. His saying: (One may suffice) i.e. we do not concede that the object sought by thought is the opinion known to correspond; why may it not be the matching opinion whose correspondence is conjectured after it occurs? His saying: (We say: rather it is sought) i.e. a turning away from what is implied, meaning we do not concede that if the non-matching opinion is not sought, it follows that the matching opinion whose correspondence is known is sought. Rather, by examining the evidence, the opinion of the ruling is sought insofar as it is an opinion, i.e. a preponderant belief with respect to it, without regard to its correspondence or lack thereof. For the primary purpose, like action in practical ijtihad, may depend on the opinion of the ruling based on the evidence. Indeed, the ruling that preponderates in the mujtahid's conjecture as being derived from the evidence must be acted upon by him without regard to its correspondence or lack thereof, especially according to those who say that every mujtahid is correct, and therefore the mistaken mujtahid is also rewarded. And it has become clear from what we have set forth for you the difference between the answer of the commentator and the answer of the author, with nothing more, and that the claim that they are identical in outcome is an illusion.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer sequence regarding what is sought by thought (al-fikr). The commentator first glosses the author's statement that the object sought by thought is the matching opinion (al-zann al-mutābiq) whose correspondence to reality is known after it occurs. The reason given is that if its correspondence were not known, it could be non-matching, making non-matching opinion sought—which is false. This would then make the opinion knowledge, since it is a decisive judgment matching reality. An objector then says: Why must the sought opinion be one whose correspondence is ْknown? Could it not be merely the matching opinion whose correspondence is conjectured (yuzann) after it occurs? The commentator responds (with 'bal') by rejecting the implication that if non-matching is not sought, then the matching-known-matching is sought. Rather, what is sought by examining the evidence is the opinion of the ruling (al-hukm) insofar as it is a preponderant belief, without attention to its correspondence or lack thereof. The primary purpose—like action in practical matters of ijtihad—depends on this opinion based on evidence. For example, the ruling that preponderates in the mujtahid's conjecture as derived from evidence must be acted upon, regardless of actual correspondence, especially on the view that every mujtahid is correct, so even the mistaken one is rewarded. The commentator concludes by highlighting the difference between his answer and the author's, noting that they are not identical in outcome.

Key Terms
المطلوب بالفكر
الظن المطابق
غلبة الظن
الاجتهاديات
المجتهد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Seeking opinion implies seeking ignorance or uncertainty.
Correction: The sought opinion is a preponderant belief based on evidence, not a groundless guess.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the object sought by thought (al-fikr) in the context of ijtihad?
A) Certain knowledge of the ruling
B) A matching opinion whose correspondence is known after it occurs
C) A preponderant belief in the ruling based on evidence, without regard to its correspondence
D) The ruling itself

Key Takeaway
In theological reasoning, the aim is a preponderant belief based on evidence, not necessarily certainty of correspondence with reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you seek to understand your religion, do you require absolute certainty before you act, or do you follow preponderant opinions from evidence? What would it take for you to act on a well-founded opinion even if you are not 100% sure?
?
The passage says that in practical matters, the primary purpose (like action) depends on preponderant belief without regard to correspondence. Are there areas in your life where you demand certainty but should be satisfied with a preponderant belief based on evidence?
?
Consider the fact that even a mistaken mujtahid is rewarded. Does your fear of being wrong hold you back from seeking knowledge and making judgments? How does this affect your approach to learning and acting?

The Definition of Zann and the Advantage of 'Ghalabat al-Zann'
Commentator explains the definition of zann and defends the phrasing 'ghalabat al-zann'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the phrase 'ghalabat al-zann' is used in the definition of zann and how preponderance is essential to its quiddity.

Core Idea
Zann is defined by an intrinsic preponderance that distinguishes it from other perceptions.

The commentator delves into the precise wording of al-Qadi's definition of zann (opinion). He explains that 'ghalabat al-zann' is not redundant but highlights that preponderance (rujhān) is a constitutive part of zann itself. This addresses a common objection and shows the semantic sophistication of the term.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to grasp the overall argument and flow.
Notice the dense commentary style; the passage contains both explanation and responses to objections.
2
Identify the key terms and their relationships
Focus on the terms zann, rujhān, and ghalabah. Understand how the commentator defines each and their mutual relation.
The commentator distinguishes between the verbal noun (masdari) meaning and the essential preponderance that serves as a differentia.
3
Understand the objection and its refutation
Someone objects that if preponderance is part of the essence, then using 'ghalabah' to refer to zann is circular. The commentator refutes this by showing existential unity.
The phrase is not a mere synonym but indicates the distinguishing feature.
4
Analyze the possessive construction
Examine why the commentator says 'in the opinion' (fī al-ẓann) and not 'it is the opinion'. This reinforces that ghalabah is a part, not the whole.
The possessive (lāmiyyah) indicates that ghalabah is a constituent part of zann.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (لأن الرجحان مأخوذ في حقيقته مقوم إياه مميز له عما عداه من أنواع الإدراك، فالمراد بالغلبة القوة والرجحان الذي هو فصل له متحد معه في الوجود لا المعنى المصدري الذي هو الاعتباري المحض ولاتحاده معه في الوجود عبر عن الظن به وبما ذكرنا ظهر اندفاع ما قيل : إن كونه مأخوذاً في حقيقته لا يصح أن يعبر به عنه، ويقام ما يطلب غلبة الظن مقام ما يطلب به الظن. قوله : (فإن ماهيته هو الاعتقاد الراجح أشار بذلك إلى أن المشتق ومبدأ الاشتقاق متحدان بالذات مختلفان بالاعتبار، كما حققه المحقق الدواني في حواشيه القديمة. قوله : ( فكأنه قيل إلخ ) فإضافة الغلبة إلى الظن ،لامية والاختصاص من حيث كونه جزءاً له مقوماً إياه، ولذا قال الشارح في الظن دون هي الظن فما قيل أن الأولي أن يقول : هي الظن ليس بشيء. قوله : ( على أن الغلبة أي (الرجحان لأن المعنى المصدري مأخوذ في ماهية الظن مقوم إياه مميز له عما عداه من الإدراكات وهذا التنبيه حصل من جعل طلبها طلبه فإن مشعر باتحادهما في الوجود فيكون ذاتياً ،له وهذا التنبيه غير مشهور وإن كان كون الظن موصوفاً بالرجحان مشهوراً، فتدبر فإنه ممازل فيه الأقدام.
His saying: (Because preponderance (al-rujhān) is taken in its quiddity (ḥaqīqah), constituting it, distinguishing it from other types of perception. So by 'predominance' (al-ghalabah) is meant strength and preponderance, which is a differentia (faṣl) for it, united with it in existence, not the verbal noun meaning which is purely relational. And because of its union with it in existence, it is expressed by it. And by what we have mentioned, the objection that 'its being taken in its quiddity does not justify expressing it by it' is refuted, and that 'what seeks predominance of opinion (ghalabat al-zann) is placed in the position of what seeks opinion.' His saying: (For its essence is preponderant belief (al-iʿtiqād al-rājiḥ). He indicated by this that the derived term and the source of derivation are unified in essence, differing in consideration, as al-Muḥaqqiq al-Dawānī verified in his old glosses. His saying: (So it is as if it were said, etc.) So the addition of 'predominance' to 'opinion' is for possession (lāmiyyah) and specification (ikhtiṣāṣ) insofar as it is a part constituting it. Hence the commentator said 'in the opinion' (fī al-ẓann) and not 'it is the opinion' (hiya al-ẓann); so what was said that it would be better to say 'it is the opinion' is nothing. His saying: (That the predominance means preponderance) because the verbal noun meaning is taken in the quiddity of opinion, constituting it, distinguishing it from other perceptions. And this attention is obtained by making seeking it seeking it, for it indicates their union in existence, so it is essential to it. And this attention is not well-known, although that opinion is described by preponderance is well-known. So ponder, for the footstep slips in it.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the definition of ẓann (opinion) and the advantage of using the phrase 'ghalabat al-ẓann' (predominance of opinion) in the definition given by al-Qāḍī. The commentator explains that preponderance (rujhān) is part of the quiddity (ḥaqīqah) of ẓann, constituting and distinguishing it from other types of perception. 'Ghalabah' here means strength and preponderance, which is a differentia (faṣl) united with the essence in existence, not a mere verbal noun. Because of this union, the term 'ẓann' can be expressed by 'ghalabah'. This refutes the objection that since the quiddity contains preponderance, it is invalid to use 'ghalabah' as a substitute. The commentator then notes that the author's phrase 'in the opinion' (fī al-ẓann) correctly indicates that 'ghalabah' is a part of the definition, not the whole, unlike if it were said 'it is the opinion'. He elaborates that the addition of 'ghalabah' to 'ẓann' is possessive (lāmiyyah), indicating that it is a constituent part. The commentator stresses that this nuance—that seeking 'ghalabah' is seeking 'ẓann'—shows their existential unity, making the preponderance essential (dhātiyy). He warns that this point is subtle and often slips.

الرجحان
غلبة الظن
الحقيقة
الفصل
الاعتقاد الراجح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that 'ghalabat al-zann' refers to a separate entity from zann, or that it is redundant.
Correction: The commentator explains that 'ghalabat al-zann' is not redundant; it highlights the internal preponderance that is essential to the very definition of zann.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator say that the phrase 'ghalabat al-zann' is used in the definition instead of just 'zann'?
A) To indicate that zann is not sufficient without preponderance
B) To emphasize that preponderance (rujhān) is an essential constituent of the quiddity of zann
C) To differentiate between two types of zann
D) To show that ghalabah is a separate entity from zann

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'ghalabat al-zann' emphasizes that preponderance is an essential part of the definition of zann, not a separate attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hold an opinion about a matter of dīn, do you actively seek out the preponderance (rujhān) that should define it, or do you let mere inclination take its place? What step will you take today to ensure your ẓann is truly based on evidence?
?
The commentator warns that 'the footstep slips' in this subtle issue. In what area of your knowledge are you most at risk of slipping—assuming you have understood when you haven't? How can you cultivate the intellectual humility this lesson demands?
?
You have just seen that the derived term and its source are unified in essence but distinct in consideration. Reflect on your own use of language in worship: do you sometimes mistake synonyms for deeper unity, or do you appreciate the precision the scholars sought? What will you change in how you speak about Allah’s attributes?

Al-Amidi's Two Properties of Thought
Al-Amidi's argument that thought has two properties and a definition need not list all properties.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Amidi's argument that thought has two properties and that a definition can validly mention only one of them.

Core Idea
A definition is valid if it captures the essence, not every property.

Al-Amidi responds to the objection that the judge's definition of thought is incomplete because it only mentions predominance of opinion. He argues that thought actually has two properties, but mentioning one in the definition suffices. This lesson explores his reasoning and its implications for defining terms.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Note the flow: al-Amidi first states that thought has two properties, then explains them, then argues that only one needs to be mentioned in a definition.
Pay attention to the parentheses: they are editorial clarifications.
2
Identify the two properties
Find the two properties: 'إفادة أصل الظن' (producing original opinion) and 'إفادة غلبة الظن' (producing predominance of opinion). Notice that the second property involves increase toward certainty.
3
Understand the key point about definitions
Al-Amidi says it is not necessary to mention all properties in a definition. Think about why: a definition aims at identification, not exhaustive enumeration.
This connects to the learning objective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وقد أجاب عنه الآمدي بأن له ) أي النظر ( خاصتين إفادة ) أصل (الظن وإفادة غلبته بأن يزداد رجحانه وقوته متقارباً إلى الجزم ) وقد اكتفى ) في تعريفه ( بذكر إحداهما ) يعني إحدى الخاصتين ) ولا يجب ذكر (الكل) أي كل خواصه في تعريفه.
His saying: (And al-Āmidī has answered about it [i.e., the objection] that it [i.e., thought] has two properties: conveying (the original) opinion and conveying its predominance, by which its preponderance and strength increase, approaching certainty. And he [al-Āmidī] sufficed in his definition with mentioning one of them, i.e., one of the two properties, and it is not necessary to mention all, i.e., all of its properties in its definition.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a direct quotation of the commentator's presentation of al-Āmidī's response to an objection. The objection was that the judge's definition of thought (al-naẓar) is not comprehensive because it only mentions 'ghalabat al-zann' (predominance of opinion) and not the original opinion (aṣl al-zann). Al-Āmidī's answer is that thought has two properties (khāṣṣatān): one is producing the original opinion (ifādat aṣl al-zann), and the other is producing its predominance (ifādat ghalabati-hi) by increasing its preponderance until it approaches certainty. In his definition, al-Āmidī sufficed with mentioning one of these two properties, and it is not obligatory to mention all properties in a definition. Thus, the definition can be validly comprehensive even if it mentions only one property.

Key Terms
النظر
خاصتين
إفادة أصل الظن
إفادة غلبة الظن
الجزم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A definition must list every property of the definiendum.
Correction: Al-Āmidī argues that mentioning one essential property suffices for a valid definition; exhaustive enumeration is not required.

Checkpoint
According to al-Āmidī, how many properties does thought (al-naẓar) have?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Al-Amidi teaches that a valid definition can capture the essence by mentioning just one essential property.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you define something important in your life—like your purpose or your connection to Allah—do you feel pressured to list every possible quality? How does Al-Amidi's insight free you to focus on the essence? What one quality would you choose?
?
Think of a time you criticized someone's incomplete understanding of an Islamic concept. Could it be that their definition was actually valid, capturing an essential property? Will you apply this lesson the next time you are tempted to demand comprehensiveness?
?
Al-Amidi shows that a definition does not need to be exhaustive. What does this teach you about how you judge your own faith? Is your acceptance of Islam based on a single essential conviction, or do you worry that you don't have every property? How will you respond to that worry now?

Defending 'Ghālibat al-ẓann' in the Definition of Nazar
The commentator explains why rajḥān is essential to ẓann, justifying the expression ghālibat al-ẓann.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why 'ghālibat al-ẓann' is not a redundant expression but essential to the definition of nazar, because rajḥān (strength) is the very differentia of ẓann.

Core Idea
Rajḥān (strength) is the very differentia of ẓann, not an addition.

The commentator addresses an objection that the definition of nazar using 'ghālibat al-ẓann' fails to capture cases where one seeks the origin of conjecture. He argues that ẓann itself is preponderant belief, so seeking 'ghālibat al-ẓann' is the same as seeking ẓann. This lesson unpacks that subtle but crucial point.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
The objection states that the definition 'seeking that by which the origin of conjecture is obtained' might exclude cases where one seeks the predominant belief itself, making the definition non-comprehensive.
The definition is from al-Qāḍī ʿAḍud al-Dīn al-Ījī.
2
Grasp the answer
The commentator asserts that ẓann is by definition preponderant belief (al-iʿtiqād al-rājiḥ). So rajḥān is its differentia, not an external property; thus 'ghālibat al-ẓann' is equivalent to ẓann.
3
Explore the linguistic nuance
The expression 'ghālibat al-ẓann' uses a partitive genitive (idāfa lāmiyya) to indicate that predominance is a constituting part of ẓann, not an accident.
This is why the commentator says 'in conjecture' not 'it is conjecture'.
4
Reflect on the deeper insight
The derived term (ẓann) and its source (rajḥān) are identical in essence but differ in aspect. This is a key insight from al-Dawānī that resolves the objection.
The commentator warns that this is a subtle point where many slip.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الظن غير أصل الظن) بلا شبهة ( فيخرج عنه ) أي عن تعريف القاضي ( ما يطلب له أصل الظن) فلا يكون تعريفه جامعاً (قلنا : الظن هو المعبر عنه بغلبة الظن، لأن الرجحان مأخوذ في حقيقته فإن ماهيته هو الاعتقاد الراجح فكأنه قيل : أو غلبة الاعتقاد التي في الظن، وفائدة العدول إلى هذه العبارة هي التنبيه على أن الغلبة أي الرجحان مأخوذة في ماهيته. قوله: (لأن الرجحان مأخوذ في حقيقته مقوم إياه مميز له عما عداه من أنواع الإدراك، فالمراد بالغلبة القوة والرجحان الذي هو فصل له متحد معه في الوجود لا المعنى المصدري الذي هو الاعتباري المحض ولاتحاده معه في الوجود عبر عن الظن به وبما ذكرنا ظهر اندفاع ما قيل : إن كونه مأخوذاً في حقيقته لا يصح أن يعبر به عنه، ويقام ما يطلب غلبة الظن مقام ما يطلب به الظن. قوله : (فإن ماهيته هو الاعتقاد الراجح أشار بذلك إلى أن المشتق ومبدأ الاشتقاق متحدان بالذات مختلفان بالاعتبار، كما حققه المحقق الدواني في حواشيه القديمة. قوله : ( فكأنه قيل إلخ ) فإضافة الغلبة إلى الظن لامية والاختصاص من حيث كونه جزءاً له مقوماً إياه، ولذا قال الشارح في الظن دون هي الظن فما قيل أن الأولي أن يقول : هي الظن ليس بشيء. قوله : ( على أن الغلبة أي الرجحان لأن المعنى المصدري مأخوذ في ماهية الظن مقوم إياه مميز له عما عداه من الإدراكات وهذا التنبيه حصل من جعل طلبها طلبه فإن مشعر باتحادهما في الوجود فيكون ذاتياً له وهذا التنبيه غير مشهور وإن كان كون الظن موصوفاً بالرجحان مشهوراً، فتدبر فإنه ممازل فيه الأقدام.
The conjecture (ẓann) other than the origin of conjecture without doubt excludes from it, i.e., from the judge's definition, that for which the origin of conjecture is sought, so his definition would not be comprehensive. We said: conjecture is what is expressed by predominance of conjecture (ghālibat al-ẓann), because strength (rajḥān) is taken into its reality, for its essence is the preponderant belief; so it is as if it were said: or the predominance of belief that is in conjecture. And the benefit of turning to this expression is to indicate that predominance, i.e., strength, is taken into its essence. He said: (Because strength is taken into its reality, constituting it, distinguishing it from other kinds of perception; so what is meant by predominance is the power and strength that is its differentia, united with it in existence, not the infinitive meaning which is purely conceptual; and because of its unity with it in existence, conjecture is expressed by it; and by what we have mentioned, the objection that it being taken into its reality does not justify expressing it by it is repelled, and what is sought by predominance of conjecture is set in place of what is sought by conjecture.) He said: (For its essence is the preponderant belief—he indicated thereby that the derived term and the source of derivation are united in essence and different in aspect, as the investigator al-Dawānī established in his old glosses.) He said: (So it is as if it were said, etc.) The addition of predominance to conjecture is partitive, and the specification is insofar as it is a constituting part of it; therefore the commentator said 'in conjecture' not 'it is conjecture'; so what is said that it would be better to say 'it is conjecture' is nothing. He said: (That predominance, i.e., strength, because the infinitive meaning is taken into the essence of conjecture, constituting it, distinguishing it from other perceptions; and this indication results from making seeking it seeking it, for it indicates their unity in existence, so it is essential to it; and this indication is not well known, although the fact that conjecture is described by strength is well known; so reflect, for it is a place where feet slip.)
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer chain defending the inclusion of 'ghālibat al-ẓann' in the definition of nazar (speculative reasoning). The objection states that if the definition uses 'that by which the origin of conjecture (aṣl al-ẓann) is sought', it excludes cases where the sought result is not the origin but the predominance of conjecture, thus making the definition non-comprehensive. The answer is that conjecture itself is nothing but preponderant belief (al-iʿtiqād al-rājiḥ); the strength (rajḥān) is not an external property but the very differentia (faṣl) of ẓann, united with it in existence. Therefore, 'ghālibat al-ẓann' is equivalent to ẓann, and seeking it is the same as seeking ẓann. The commentator then clarifies: the benefit of using the expression 'ghālibat al-ẓann' is to draw attention to the fact that rajḥān is part of the essence. He further explains that the derived term (ẓann) and its source (rajḥān) are identical in essence but distinct in consideration, quoting al-Dawānī. The addition of 'ghāliba' to 'ẓann' is partitive (lāmiyya), meaning the predominance is a constituent part of ẓann. Finally, he notes that this subtlety is not commonly recognized, but it is crucial for correctly understanding the definition.

Key Terms
الظن
غلبة الظن
الرجحان
الماهية
المشتق ومبدأ الاشتقاق
الخاصة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That ghālibat al-ẓann is merely a property of ẓann, not its essence.
Correction: The commentator argues that rajḥān (strength) is the differentia of ẓann, making it essential to its definition, not an accidental property.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator argue that 'ghālibat al-ẓann' can be used in the definition of nazar?
A) Because it is a more precise expression for the same thing.
B) Because rajḥān is the differentia of ẓann and united with it in existence.
C) Because the opponent already accepts it.
D) Because it avoids the problem of infinite regress.

Key Takeaway
Rajḥān is the differentia of ẓann, making 'ghālibat al-ẓann' an equivalent expression, not a mere property.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In the lesson, the commentator emphasizes that rajḥān (strength) is not an extra feature but the very differentia of ẓann. In what area of your faith have you been content with a weak, unexamined belief that lacks true preponderance? What will you do this week to seek the stronger foundation that nazar provides?
?
The passage warns that this subtlety is 'a place where feet slip'. When you encounter theological arguments, do you tend to accept them based on their surface appeal or do you rigorously test whether the evidence truly gives you rajḥān? Are you willing to take up the practice of nazar to ensure your convictions are not built on shaky ground?
?
If your most cherished beliefs about Allah were challenged, would your conviction be at the level of ghālibat al-ẓann – a preponderant belief that has been thoroughly investigated – or merely a weak ẓann inherited without verification? What specific step can you take today to strengthen one aspect of your faith to the level of preponderance?
